**Critical observation:** The GT contains `sin(log(A + 1))`, which is a very specific basis function. None of the candidates contain `sin(log(...))`. Let me check what basis functions the candidates use:

Looking through all candidates, I see combinations of:
- Rational functions: `A/(A+c)`, `1/(A+c)`, `A²/(A+c)`
- Logarithms: `log(A*c + 1)`
- Exponentials: `exp(A*c)`
- Sine: `sin(A*c + c)`
- Power: `A**c`
- Products like `A*log(...)/(A+c)`

**The GT has `sin(log(A+1))`** - a sine of a logarithm. This is a fundamentally different basis function from `sin(A*c + c)` (sine of a linear function) or `log(A*c + 1)` alone.

`sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as any finite combination of:
- Polynomials/rational functions of A
- `log(A+c)` terms
- `sin(linear in A)` terms  
- `exp(linear in A)` terms
- Power functions `A^c`

These are all linearly independent function classes. The function `sin(log(A+1))` has a unique oscillatory behavior that decays in frequency as A increases (since log grows slowly), which is qualitatively different from `sin(cA)` which has constant frequency.

No candidate contains `sin(log(...))`, so no candidate can match the GT exactly. Let me verify there's no clever algebraic trick I'm missing by checking each candidate type:

- Candidates with `sin(A*c + c)`: These oscillate with constant frequency in A, while `sin(log(A+1))` has decreasing frequency. **Cannot match.**
- Candidates with only rational/polynomial/log/exp terms: These cannot produce oscillatory `sin(log(...))` behavior. **Cannot match.**
- Candidates with `t` dependence: GT has no `t` dependence, so `t`-dependent terms must vanish. But even then, remaining terms don't have `sin(log(...))`. **Cannot match.**

Let me verify each candidate:

Candidates 1-50 all use combinations of rational functions, polynomials, `log(A*c+1)`, `sin(A*c+c)`, `exp(A*c)`, and `A^c`. None contain `sin(log(...))`.
